  3: "And... there are moments when I\'ll enter a dark room, just before I turn on the lights, when I swear I\'m not alone. I have this inescapable sensation that I\'ve entered into a space that belongs to someone else... Or <i>something</i> else."

  3: "Voices, shadows, strange lights... a presence. Not a ghost, but something bigger. Something older. A kind of Power that thrummed in the air all around me."
  3: "I should have been terrified, but for some reason, I wasn\'t. It didn\'t feel malicious at all. Mostly it seemed curious. Even... playful?"
  3: "This place is strange. But there\'s a beauty here, too. And now that I have the house fixed up, I finally have the time to get to know it."

  3: "We took a stroll down by the river, and almost had a nice time. Unfortunately, since I have no intention of selling my land, our conversation quickly turned into an argument. I told him to get off my property and stormed away."
  3: "Then I heard a splash."
  3: "I turned around just in time to see him vanish under the water. I thought he must have tripped at first, but I\'ve been replaying the moment in my head, and the more I do, the more convinced I am that what actually happened is, the river rose up and grabbed him."
  3: "I leapt in after him, but by the time I got the poor fool to shore, he was half-drowned and completely terrified. Without another word, he ran to his car and drove off."
  3: "I don\'t know why, but I\'m positive that what happened was my doing. The Power in this place... it was responding to <i>my</i> anger. I\'m connected to it, somehow."

  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "Ever since that incident with the man from the development group, I\'ve been searching for answers... following some sixth sense I don\'t understand on longer and longer journeys into the woods."

  3: "From the moment I arrived, the place felt... wrong. Sick, somehow. The light didn\'t behave the way light is supposed to. Against every instinct, I crept closer, and peered in through a window."
  3: "It was dark inside, and hazy. There were cobwebs everywhere, and roots growing up through the walls. But I could make out a shape. Something standing in the corner. It looked almost like a person..."
  3: "And then it turned around. And it was NOT a person."
  3: "I\'ve never run so hard in my life."

  3: "It\'s a Sunday evening. Chilly. I\'m sitting on the deck, watching the sunset through the trees, thinking about everything I now know. And what comes next."
  3: "Cora says there\'s a Power that flows through these woods, pooling in places like the ruins near Westchester, and the river near my home. She says it calls out to those who can hear it. Those like her... and me."
  3: "But there\'s even more she doesn\'t say, because she doesn\'t need to. I can feel it, this Power. It\'s bigger than all of us... a swift-moving river so wide you can\'t see the shore and so deep you can\'t touch the bottom."
  3: "It\'s not good or evil, but it is volatile. It responds to intention. Cora says that those who respect it, who nurture and protect it, can use it to do good things."
  3: "But what about those who don\'t?"

How that corruption has rippled down over the years. So many lives broken. So many innocent people hurt."
  3: "Was it malice that drove him? Or just arrogant, selfish ignorance?"
  3: "I guess there\'s no difference in the end..."
  3: "I told Cora about the development group sniffing around my land, and the two of us are agreed: they absolutely cannot be allowed to build here."
  3: "This river must be protected. So I will be the one to protect it."
  3: ""

They\'re persistent, I\'ll give them that. They\'re buying up all the land around here. And they still want mine."
  3: "Which means that every day, I see his car come down the drive. Every day, I hear his footsteps on the porch, his knock on the door, three times, tap-tap-tap. Every day I see his smiling face through the screen, straightening his little bowtie and taking off his little hat."

  3: "But I <i>can\'t</i> fall for him! He works for the development group that wants to rip this forest apart, and I can\'t let that happen. The river that runs through my land, and the Power within it, have to be protected from these people."
  3: "But they also need protected from it. The Power won\'t just let them do as they please. I can already feel it starting to get restless. Agitated.   3: "Where does it stop? How does it end? Who gets hurt, before this is over?"
  3: "I keep circling back to a very dumb idea: What if I just told him the truth? Cora made me promise I wouldn\'t tell anyone about the Power, but... could I make him understand? Could he make THEM understand?"

  3: "He thought I was pulling his leg at first, so I took him to the ruins near Westchester. I made him walk up and look in the window."

  3: "The next day he confronted the development group. I can only imagine what dramatic speech he made them, but whatever he said got through. They\'re pulling back the trucks, slowing down construction, and redrawing their plans to better protect the river."
